6> what does εμπιστεύομαι mean in ancient greek? and how do you pronounce it?

"Εμπιστεύομαι" (empiteúomai) in Ancient Greek means "to trust" or "to have confidence in." The pronunciation of this verb is roughly "em-pee-STEW-oh-my."

15> great! thanks! are there any other major parts of speech to know about? we have covered nouns, verbs, adverbs, adjectives, prepositions.  is there anything else?

Yes, there are a few more parts of speech that are important to know about:

1. Conjunction - a word that connects words, phrases, clauses, or sentences.
2. Interjection - a word or phrase used to express strong emotion, such as surprise, anger, or joy.
3. Pronoun - a word that takes the place of a noun in a sentence.
4. Article - a word used before a noun to indicate the presence and type of reference being made to the noun.

In ancient Greek, the use of conjunctions, interjections, pronouns, and articles is similar to their use in modern English, so learning these parts of speech would help you
 understand and communicate in ancient Greek more effectively.

20> great! could you show me 40 articles?

Sure! In Ancient Greek, there are only two articles: the definite article "the" and the indefinite article "a/an". The definite article in Ancient Greek is declined based o
n gender, number, and case, so there are different forms for different contexts. Here are the forms of the definite article:

Masculine:
Singular: ὁ (ho)
Plural: οἱ (hoi)

Feminine:
Singular: ἡ (hē)
Plural: αἱ (hai)

Neuter:
Singular: τό (to)
Plural: τά (ta)

The indefinite article "a/an" is usually expressed through the use of the numeral "one" (εἷς or μία in the masculine and feminine respectively, and εἷς in the neuter). For 
example: "one man" would translate as "ἄνδρας εἷς".

1> could you please teach me 40 mathematical terms in ancient greek along with their pronunciations and english names?

Sure, here are 40 ancient Greek mathematical terms along with their pronunciations and English names:

Sure, here are 40 words related to mathematics in Ancient Greek:

Περιφέρεια (Peripheria) - Periphery - The outer bound or surface of a circle
Γωνία (Gonia) - Angle - The space between two lines that meet at a point
Διάμετρος (Diametros) - Diameter - A straight line passing through the center of a circle or sphere
Κύκλος (Kyklos) - Circle - A closed plane figure with all points equidistant from the center
Επιφάνεια (Epiphanai) - Surface - The outermost layer of a solid object
Ελάχιστον (Elachiston) - Minimum - The smallest value in a set of numbers
Μέγιστον (Megiston) - Maximum - The largest value in a set of numbers
Πλάτος (Platos) - Width - The distance from side to side of a object
Μήκος (Mikos) - Length - The distance from one end to another

1. ἀνατομία - anatomía - anatomy - from ἀνατέμνω (anatémno), "to cut up, to dissect"
2. σκελετικός - skeletikós - skeletal - from σκελετός (skeletós), "dried up, withered"
3. μυελικός - myelikós - myelic - from μυελός (myelós), "marrow"
4. καρδιακός - kardiakós - cardiac - from καρδία (kardía), "heart"
5. νεφρικός - nephrikós - nephric - from νεφρός (nephros), "kidney"
6. γαστρικός - gastrikós - gastric - from γαστήρ (gastér), "stomach"
7. εντερικός - enterikós - enteric - from εντερικός (enterikós), "pertaining to the intestines"
8. μυοσκελετικός - myoskeletikós - musculoskeletal - from μύος (mýos), "muscle" and σκελετός (skeletós), "dried up, withered"
9. σπονδυλικός - spondylikós - spinal - from σπονδύλιος (spondylios), "vertebral"
10. πνευματικός - pneumatikós - respiratory - from πνεῦμα (pneuma), "air, breath"
11. ιστιακός - istiakós - venous - from ἰστή (istē), "vein"
12. αρτηριακός - artēriakós - arterial - from ἀρτηρία (artēria), "artery"
13. νευρικός - neyrikós - nervous - from νεῦρον (neuron), "nerve"
14. οστεοανατομικός - osteoanatomikós - osteoanatomical - from ὀστέον (osteon), "bone" and ἀνατομία (anatomía), "anatomy"
15. σαρκωτικός - sarkōtikós - fleshy - from σάρξ (sarx), "flesh"
16. καρδιοανα

23. στεφανιακός - stefaniakós - crown-shaped - from στέφανος (stéfanos), "crown, wreath"
24. μαστιγικός - masigikós - painful - from μαστίζω (mastízo), "to whip, to beat"
25. χειρουργικός - cheirourgikós - surgical - from χειρουργία (cheirourgía), "surgery"
